# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

58-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've successfully analyzed the Prometheus repository and identified all Go source files that implement web UI authentication. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Key Findings:

**Three Core Authentication Mechanisms in Prometheus:**

1. **BasicAuth Middleware** - Configured via `--web.config.file` flag with bcrypt-hashed passwords
2. **TLS Client Certificate Validation** - Also configured in the web config file with `client_auth_type` and `client_ca_file` options  
3. **Admin API Access Control** - Controlled by the `--web.enable-admin-api` flag, protecting delete_series, snapshot, and clean_tombstones endpoints

**Core Files Identified:**
- `web/web.go` - Main HTTP handler that initializes and runs the server with middleware
- `cmd/prometheus/main.go` - Command-line flag parsing for web configuration
- `web/api/v1/api.go` - API implementation with admin endpoint access control checks

**Authentication Flow:**
The web configuration file path flows from the command-line flag → passed to handler.Run() → forwarded to toolkit_web.ServeMultiple() which applies TLS and BasicAuth middleware. Admin endpoints independently verify the enableAdmin flag before allowing operations.

The complete findings have been written to `/workspace/answer.json` with detailed file paths, symbols, execution chain, and comprehensive narrative explanation.

\n117: var fgprofHandler = fgprof.Handler()\n118: \n119: // withStackTracer logs the stack trace in case the request panics. The function\n120: // will re-raise the error which will then be handled by the net/http package.\n121: // It is needed because the go-kit log package doesn't manage properly the\n122: // panics from net/http (see https://github.com/go-kit/kit/issues/233).\n123: func withStackTracer(h http.Handler, l *slog.Logger) http.Handler {\n124: \treturn http.HandlerFunc(func(w http.ResponseWriter, r buf[:runtime.Stack(buf, false)]\n130: \t\t\t\tl.Error(\"panic while serving request\", \"client\", r.RemoteAddr, \"url\", r.URL, \"err\", err, \"stack\", buf)\n131: \t\t\t\tpanic(err)\n132: \t\t\t}\n133: \t\t}()\n134: \t\th.ServeHTTP(w, r)\n135: \t})\n136: }\n137: \n138: type metrics struct {\n139: \trequestCounter  *prometheus.CounterVec\n140: \trequestDuration These endpoints are:\\n   - `deleteSeries()` (web/api/v1/api.go:2026-2057): Checks if api.enableAdmin is false, returns error \\\"admin APIs disabled\\\"\\n   - `snapshot()` (web/api/v1/api.go:2059-2091): Checks if api.enableAdmin is false, returns error \\\"admin APIs disabled\\\"\\n   - `cleanTombstones()` (web/api/v1/api.go:2093-2102): Checks if api.enableAdmin is false, returns error \\\"admin APIs disabled\\\"\\n\\nThe enableAdmin flag is controlled by the `--web.enable-admin-api` command-line flag (cmd/prometheus/main.go:430-431), which defaults to false.\\n\\nThe authentication flow works as follows:\\n1.
